    Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-21
   </h1>

      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-21
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">
        Микоян и Гуревич МиГ-21
       </span>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/NATO_reporting_name" title="NATO reporting name">
        NATO reporting name
       </a>
       :
       <b>
        Fishbed
       </b>
       ) is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supersonic" title="Supersonic">
        supersonic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">
        jet
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">
        fighter
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Interceptor_aircraft" title="Interceptor aircraft">
        interceptor aircraft
       </a>
       , designed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan" title="Mikoyan">
        Mikoyan-Gurevich
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/OKB" title="OKB">
        Design Bureau
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       . It was popularly nicknamed "balalaika", from the aircraft's planform-view resemblance to the
       <a href="/wiki/Balalaika" title="Balalaika">
        Russian stringed musical instrument
       </a>
       or
       <i>
        ołówek
       </i>
       (English:
       <span lang="en" xml:lang="en">
        pencil
       </span>
       ) by Polish pilots due to the shape of its
       <a href="/wiki/Fuselage" title="Fuselage">
        fuselage
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Approximately 60 countries over four continents have flown the MiG-21, and it still serves many nations six decades after its maiden flight. It made aviation records, became
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-produced_aircraft" title="List of most-produced aircraft">
        the most-produced supersonic jet aircraft in aviation history
       </a>
       , the most-produced combat aircraft since the
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">
        Korean War
       </a>
       and previously the longest production run of a combat aircraft (now exceeded by both the
       <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_F-15_Eagle" title="McDonnell Douglas F-15 Eagle">
        McDonnell Douglas F-15 Eagle
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">
        General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

            <span class="tocnumber">
             5.3
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Use as space launch platform
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">
         <a href="#Specifications_(MiG-21-93)">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           6
          </span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32">

          </span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33">
         <a href="#References">
          <span class="tocnumber">

          </span>
         </a>
         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34">

            </span>

          </li>

      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Development">
        Development
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Development">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">
        Origins
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The MiG-21 jet fighter was a continuation of Soviet jet fighters, starting with the subsonic
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-15" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-15">
        MiG-15
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-17" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-17">
        MiG-17
       </a>
       , and the supersonic
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-19" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-19">
        MiG-19
       </a>
       . A number of experimental Mach 2 Soviet designs were based on nose intakes with either swept-back wings, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-7" title="Sukhoi Su-7">
        Sukhoi Su-7
       </a>
       , or tailed
       <a href="/wiki/Delta_wing" title="Delta wing">
        deltas
       </a>
       , of which the MiG-21 would be the most successful.
      </p>
      <p>
       Development of what would become the MiG-21 began in the early 1950s, when Mikoyan OKB finished a preliminary design study for a
       <a href="/wiki/Prototype" title="Prototype">
        prototype
       </a>
       designated Ye-1 in 1954. This project was very quickly reworked when it was determined that the planned engine was underpowered; the redesign led to the second prototype, the Ye-2. Both these and other early prototypes featured swept wings. The first prototype with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delta_wings" title="Delta wings">
        delta wings
       </a>
       as found on production variants was the Ye-4. It made its maiden flight on 16 June 1955 and its first public appearance during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Aviation_Day" title="Soviet Aviation Day">
        Soviet Aviation Day display
       </a>
       at Moscow's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tushino_airfield" title="Tushino airfield">
        Tushino airfield
       </a>
       in July 1956.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the West, due to the lack of available information, early details of the MiG-21 often were confused with those of similar Soviet fighters of the era. In one instance,
       <i>
        Jane's All the World's Aircraft 1960–1961
       </i>
       listed the "Fishbed" as a Sukhoi design and used an illustration of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-9" title="Sukhoi Su-9">
        Su-9 'Fishpot'
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Design">
        Design
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Design">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis,_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis%2C_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg/220px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis%2C_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis%2C_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg/330px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis%2C_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis%2C_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg/440px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis%2C_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis,_Hungary_-_Air_Force_AN0740836.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Air_Force" title="Hungarian Air Force">
          Hungarian Air Force
         </a>
         MiG-21bis on takeoff.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mig-21.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mig-21.jpg/220px-Mig-21.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mig-21.jpg/330px-Mig-21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mig-21.jpg/440px-Mig-21.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mig-21.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         MiG-21 at Aleksotas Airport (S. Dariaus / S. Gireno), Kaunas (EYKS)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MiG-21M_Preschen_(22951457305).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="933" data-file-width="1400" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/MiG-21M_Preschen_%2822951457305%29.jpg/220px-MiG-21M_Preschen_%2822951457305%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/MiG-21M_Preschen_%2822951457305%29.jpg/330px-MiG-21M_Preschen_%2822951457305%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/MiG-21M_Preschen_%2822951457305%29.jpg/440px-MiG-21M_Preschen_%2822951457305%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MiG-21M_Preschen_(22951457305).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         MiG-21М National People's Army of the GDR, August 1990
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The MiG-21 was the first successful Soviet aircraft combining
       <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">
        fighter
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Interceptor_aircraft" title="Interceptor aircraft">
        interceptor
       </a>
       characteristics in a single aircraft. It was a lightweight fighter, achieving Mach 2 with a relatively low-powered
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afterburner_(engine)" title="Afterburner (engine)">
        afterburning
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Turbojet" title="Turbojet">
        turbojet
       </a>
       , and is thus comparable to the American
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_F-104_Starfighter" title="Lockheed F-104 Starfighter">
        Lockheed F-104 Starfighter
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Northrop_F-5" title="Northrop F-5">
        Northrop F-5 Freedom Fighter
       </a>
       and the French
       <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_III" title="Dassault Mirage III">
        Dassault Mirage III
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_2008_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gordon_2008-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its basic layout was used for numerous other Soviet designs; delta-winged aircraft included
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-9" title="Sukhoi Su-9">
        Su-9
       </a>
       interceptor and the fast
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_Ye-150_family" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich Ye-150 family">
        E-150
       </a>
       prototype from MiG bureau while the mass-produced successful front fighter
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-7" title="Sukhoi Su-7">
        Su-7
       </a>
       and Mikoyan's
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_I-75" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich I-75">
        I-75
       </a>
       experimental interceptor combined a similar fuselage shape with swept-back wings. However, the characteristic layout with the shock cone and front air intake did not see widespread use outside the USSR and finally proved to have limited development potential, mainly because of the very small space available for the radar.
      </p>
      <p>
       Like many aircraft designed as interceptors, the MiG-21 had a short range. This was exacerbated by the poor placement of the internal fuel tanks ahead of the centre of gravity. As the internal fuel was consumed, the center of gravity would shift rearward beyond acceptable parameters. This had the effect of making the plane
       <a href="/wiki/Longitudinal_static_stability" title="Longitudinal static stability">
        statically unstable
       </a>
       to the point of being difficult to control, resulting in an endurance of only 45 minutes in clean condition. This can be somewhat countered by carrying fuel in external tanks closer to the center of gravity. The Chinese variants somewhat improved the internal fuel tank layout (also second generation of Soviet variants), and also carry significantly larger external fuel tanks to counter this issue.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, when more than half the fuel was used up, violent maneuvers prevented fuel from flowing into the engine (questionable), thereby causing it to shut down in flight. This increased the risk of tank implosions (MiG-21 had tanks pressurized with air from the engine's compressor), a problem inherited from the
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-15" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-15">
        MiG-15
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-17" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-17">
        MiG-17
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-19" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-19">
        MiG-19
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J_F_Dunnigan_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-J_F_Dunnigan-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The short endurance and low fuel capacity of the MiG-21F, PF, PFM, S/SM and M/MF variants—though each had a somewhat greater fuel capacity than its predecessor—led to the development of the MT and SMT variants. These had an increased range of 250 km (155 mi) compared to the MiG-21SM, but at the cost of worsening all other performance figures, such as a lower service ceiling and slower time to altitude.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_2008_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gordon_2008-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM,_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1024" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM%2C_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg/220px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM%2C_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM%2C_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg/330px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM%2C_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM%2C_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg/440px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM%2C_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PFM,_Russia_-_Air_Force_AN1343184.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A pole mounted MIG-21
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The delta wing, while excellent for a fast-climbing interceptor, meant any form of turning combat led to a rapid loss of speed. However, the light loading of the aircraft could mean that a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climb_rate" title="Climb rate">
        climb rate
       </a>
       of 235 m/s (46,250 ft/min) was possible with a combat-loaded MiG-21bis,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_2008_1-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gordon_2008-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       not far short of the performance of the later
       <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">
        F-16A
       </a>
       . Given a skilled pilot and capable missiles, it could give a good account of itself against contemporary fighters. Its G-limits were increased from +7Gs in initial variants to +8.5Gs in the latest variants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MiG-21BIS_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-MiG-21BIS-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was replaced by the newer variable-geometry
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-23" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-23">
        MiG-23
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan_MiG-27" title="Mikoyan MiG-27">
        MiG-27
       </a>
       for ground support duties. However, not until the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-29" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-29">
        MiG-29
       </a>
       would the Soviet Union ultimately replace the MiG-21 as a maneuvering dogfighter to counter new American air superiority types.
      </p>
      <p>
       The MiG-21 was exported widely and remains in use. The aircraft's simple controls, engine, weapons, and avionics were typical of Soviet-era military designs. The use of a tail with the delta wing aids stability and control at the extremes of the
       <a href="/wiki/Flight_envelope" title="Flight envelope">
        flight envelope
       </a>
       , enhancing safety for lower-skilled pilots; this in turn enhanced its marketability in exports to developing countries with limited training programs and restricted pilot pools. While technologically inferior to the more advanced fighters it often faced, low production and maintenance costs made it a favorite of nations buying
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">
        Eastern Bloc
       </a>
       military hardware. Several Russian, Israeli and Romanian firms have begun to offer upgrade packages to MiG-21 operators, designed to bring the aircraft up to a modern standard, with greatly upgraded avionics and armaments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_2008_1-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gordon_2008-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">
        Production
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Production">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1108" data-file-width="1379" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG/220px-MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG/330px-MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG/440px-MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MiG-21F-13_Fishbed_C.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Czechoslovak MiG-21F-13 "Fishbed C"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A total of 10,645 aircraft were built in the USSR. They were produced in three factories: AZ 30
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [N 1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (3,203 aircraft) in Moscow (also known as
       <i>
        MMZ Znamya Truda
       </i>
       ), GAZ 21 (5,765 aircraft) in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gorky_(city)" title="Gorky (city)">
        Gorky
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [N 2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and TAZ 31 (1,678 aircraft) in
       <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">
        Tbilisi
       </a>
       . Generally, Gorky built single-seaters for the Soviet forces. Moscow constructed single-seaters for export, and Tbilisi manufactured the twin-seaters both for export and the USSR, though there were exceptions. The MiG-21R and MiG-21bis for export and for the USSR were built in Gorky, 17 single-seaters were helmed in Tbilisi (MiG-21 and MiG-21F), the MiG-21MF was first constructed in Moscow and then Gorky, and the MiG-21U was built in Moscow as well as in Tbilisi.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_2008_1-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gordon_2008-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Gorky
        </th>
        <td>
         83 MiG-21F; 513 MiG-21F-13; 525 MiG-21PF; 233 MiG-21PFL; 944 MiG-21PFS/PFM; 448 MiG-21R; 145 MiG-21S/SN; 349 MiG-21SM; 281 MiG-21SMT; 2013 MiG-21bis; 231 MiG-21MF
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         Moscow
        </th>
        <td>
         MiG-21U (all export units); MiG-21PF (all export units); MiG-21FL (all units not built by HAL); MiG-21M (all); 15 MiG-21MT (all)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         Tbilisi
        </th>
        <td>
         17 MiG-21 and MiG-21F; 181 MiG-21U
         <i>
          izdeliye
         </i>
         66–400 and 66–600 (1962–1966); 347 MiG-21US (1966–1970); 1133 MiG-21UM (1971 to end)
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       A total of 194 MiG-21F-13s were built under licence in Czechoslovakia, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindustan_Aeronautics_Ltd." title="Hindustan Aeronautics Ltd.">
        Hindustan Aeronautics Ltd.
       </a>
       of India built 657 MiG-21FL, MiG-21M and MiG-21bis (of which 225 were bis)
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Design_2">
        Design
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Design">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MiG-21_cockpit.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Premodern MiG-21 cockpit
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1296" data-file-width="1936" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg/220px-Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg/330px-Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg/440px-Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cockpit_MiG_21_F_13.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         MiG-21F-13 cockpit at the Aviation Museum in Bucharest, Romania
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1296" data-file-width="1936" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG/220px-Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG/330px-Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG/440px-Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Back_of_a_MiG-21.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         MiG-21F-13 rear view
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The MiG-21 has a
       <a href="/wiki/Delta_wing" title="Delta wing">
        delta wing
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweep_angle" title="Sweep angle">
        sweep angle
       </a>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Leading_edge" title="Leading edge">
        leading edge
       </a>
       is 57° with a
       <a href="/wiki/TsAGI" title="TsAGI">
        TsAGI
       </a>
       S-12
       <a href="/wiki/Airfoil" title="Airfoil">
        airfoil
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Angle_of_incidence_(aerodynamics)" title="Angle of incidence (aerodynamics)">
        angle of incidence
       </a>
       is 0° while the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dihedral_(aircraft)" title="Dihedral (aircraft)">
        dihedral angle
       </a>
       is −2°. On the
       <a href="/wiki/Trailing_edge" title="Trailing edge">
        trailing edge
       </a>
       there are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ailerons" title="Ailerons">
        ailerons
       </a>
       with an area of 1.18 m², and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flap_(aircraft)" title="Flap (aircraft)">
        flaps
       </a>
       with an area of 1.87 m². In front of the ailerons there are small
       <a href="/wiki/Wing_fence" title="Wing fence">
        wing fences
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The fuselage is
       <a href="/wiki/Semi-monocoque" title="Semi-monocoque">
        semi-monocoque
       </a>
       with an elliptical profile and a maximum width of 1.24 m (4 ft 1 in). The air flow to the engine is regulated by an
       <a href="/wiki/Inlet_cone" title="Inlet cone">
        inlet cone
       </a>
       in the air intake. On early model MiG-21s, the cone has three positions. For speeds up to Mach 1.5 the cone is fully retracted to the maximum aft position. For speeds between Mach 1.5 and Mach 1.9 the cone moves to the middle position. For speeds higher than Mach 1.9 the cone moves to the maximum forward position. On the later model MiG-21PF, the intake cone moves to a position based on the actual speed. The cone position for a given speed is calculated by the UVD-2M system using air pressures from in front and behind the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_compressor" title="Gas compressor">
        compressor
       </a>
       of the engine. On both sides of the nose there are gills to supply the engine with more air while on the ground and during takeoff. In the first variant of the MiG-21, the
       <a href="/wiki/Pitot_tube" title="Pitot tube">
        pitot tube
       </a>
       is attached to the bottom of the nose. After the MiG-21P variant, this tube is attached to the top of the air intake. Later versions shifted the pitot tube attachment point 15 degrees to the right, as seen from the cockpit and had an emergency pitot head on the right side, just ahead of the canopy and below the pilot's eyeline.
      </p>
      <p>
       The cabin is pressurized and air conditioned. On variants prior to the MiG-21PFM, the cabin canopy is hinged at the front. When ejecting, the SK-1 ejection seat connects with the canopy to make a capsule that encloses the pilot. The capsule protects the pilot from the high-speed airflow encountered during high-speed ejections. After ejection, the capsule opens to allow the pilot to parachute to the ground. However, ejecting at low altitudes can cause the canopy to take too long to separate, sometimes resulting in pilot death. The minimum height for ejection
       <b>
        in level flight
       </b>
       was 110 m. Starting from the MiG-21PFM, the canopy is hinged on the right side of the cockpit.
      </p>
      <p>
       On the under side of the aircraft there are three air brakes, two at the front and one at the rear. The front air brakes have an area of 0.76 m², and a deflection angle of 35°. The rear air brake has an area of 0.46 m² and a deflection angle of 40°. The rear air brake is blocked if the airplane carries an external fuel tank. Behind the air brakes are the bays for the main landing gear. On the under side of the airplane, just behind the trailing edge of the wing are attachment points for two
       <a href="/wiki/JATO" title="JATO">
        JATO
       </a>
       rockets. The front section of the fuselage ends at
       <a href="/wiki/Former" title="Former">
        former
       </a>
       #28. The rear section of the fuselage starts at former #28a and is removable for engine maintenance.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Empennage" title="Empennage">
        empennage
       </a>
       of the MiG-21 consists of a
       <a href="/wiki/Vertical_stabilizer" title="Vertical stabilizer">
        vertical stabilizer
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Stabilator" title="Stabilator">
        stabilator
       </a>
       and a small fin on the bottom of the tail to improve yaw control. The vertical stabilizer has a sweep angle of 60° and an area of 5.32 m² (on earlier version 3.8 m²) and a
       <a href="/wiki/Rudder" title="Rudder">
        rudder
       </a>
       . The stabilator has a sweep angle of 57°, an area of 3.94 m² and a span of 2.6 m.
      </p>
      <p>
       The MiG-21 uses a
       <a href="/wiki/Tricycle" title="Tricycle">
        tricycle
       </a>
       type undercarriage. On most variants the main landing gear uses tires that are 800 mm in diameter and 200 mm in width. Only the MiG-21F variants use tires with the size 660x200 mm. The wheels of the main landing gear retract into the fuselage after rotating 87° and the shock absorbers retract into the wing. The nose gear retracts forward into the fuselage under the radar. The nose wheel can be lowered manually by simply unlocking its hatch from inside the cockpit. Thus, landing with undercarriage locked in the up position due to an internal failure was not a major issue, with a number of such successful landings on the nosewheel + ventral fuel tank or the airbrake.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_history">
        Operational history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Operational history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="India">
        India
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: India">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sheeju_mig21.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Sheeju_mig21.JPG/220px-Sheeju_mig21.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Sheeju_mig21.JPG/330px-Sheeju_mig21.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Sheeju_mig21.JPG/440px-Sheeju_mig21.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sheeju_mig21.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">
          IAF
         </a>
         MiG-21 Bison
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       India is the third largest operator of MiG-21s, behind Russia and China. In 1961, the
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">
        Indian Air Force
       </a>
       (IAF) opted to purchase the MiG-21 over several other Western competitors. As part of the deal, the Soviet Union offered India full transfer of technology and rights for local assembly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Santosh_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Santosh-8">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1964, the MiG-21 became the first supersonic fighter jet to enter service with the IAF. Due to limited induction numbers and lack of pilot training, the IAF MiG-21 played a limited role in the
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1965" title="Indo-Pakistani War of 1965">
        Indo-Pakistani War of 1965
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canberra_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Canberra-9">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the IAF gained valuable experience while operating the MiG-21 for defensive sorties during the war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canberra_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Canberra-9">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The positive feedback from IAF pilots during the 1965 war prompted India to place more orders for the fighter jet and also invest heavily in building the MiG-21's maintenance infrastructure and pilot training programs.
      </p>
      <p>
       Since 1963, India has introduced more than 1,200 MiG fighters into its air force. As of August 2013, at least 252 MiG-21s are known to be in operation. However, the plane has been plagued by safety problems. Since 1970 more than 170 Indian pilots and 40 civilians have been killed in MiG-21 accidents. At least 14 MiG-21s have crashed between 2010 and 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Over half of the 840 aircraft built between 1966 and 1984 were lost to crashes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When in afterburner, the engine operates very close to its surge line and the ingestion of even a small bird can lead to an engine surge/seizure and flame out.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 11 December 2013, India's second generation supersonic jet fighter, MiG-21FL was decommissioned after being in service for 50 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In view of the several incidents that have occurred after the 1999 Kargil War, the modernized MiG-21 Bison seems to have at present the role of an interceptor and possibly a limited role of a fighter aircraft.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The remaining MiG-21 Bisons of the IAF are scheduled to be phased out by 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1971_India_Pakistan_War">
        1971 India Pakistan War
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1971 India Pakistan War">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The expansion of IAF MiG-21 fleet marked a developing India-Soviet Union military partnership, which enabled India to field a formidable air force to counter Chinese and Pakistani threats.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-16">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The capabilities of the MiG-21 were put to the test during the
       <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War" title="Bangladesh Liberation War">
        Bangladesh Liberation War
       </a>
       . During the war, the MiG-21s played a crucial role in giving the IAF air superiority over vital points and areas in the western theater of the conflict.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 1971 war witnessed the first supersonic air combat in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subcontinent" title="Subcontinent">
        subcontinent
       </a>
       when an Indian MiG-21FLs claimed a
       <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Air_Force" title="Pakistan Air Force">
        PAF
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_F-104_Starfighter" title="Lockheed F-104 Starfighter">
        F-104 Starfighter
       </a>
       with its GSh-23 twin-barrelled 23 mm cannon.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the time the hostilities came to an end, the IAF MiG-21s had claimed four PAF F-104s, two PAF
       <a href="/wiki/Shenyang_J-6" title="Shenyang J-6">
        Shenyang F-6
       </a>
       , one PAF
       <a href="/wiki/North_American_F-86_Sabre" title="North American F-86 Sabre">
        North American F-86 Sabre
       </a>
       and one PAF
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_C-130_Hercules" title="Lockheed C-130 Hercules">
        Lockheed C-130 Hercules
       </a>
       . According to one Western military analyst, the MiG-21s had clearly "won" the much anticipated air combat between the MiG-21 and the F-104 Starfighter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coggins_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Coggins-19">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of the formidable performance of the MiG-21s, several nations, including
       <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">
        Iraq
       </a>
       , approached India for MiG-21 pilot training. By the early 1970s, more than 120 Iraqi pilots were being trained by the Indian Air Force.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-20">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kargil_War_and_Atlantique_incident">
        Kargil War and Atlantique incident
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kargil War and Atlantique incident">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       It was also used as late as 1999 in the
       <a href="/wiki/Kargil_War" title="Kargil War">
        Kargil War
       </a>
       , in which one
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">
        Indian Air Force
       </a>
       MiG-21s was destroyed by ground fire.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The MiG-21's last known kill took place in 1999 during the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantique_incident" title="Atlantique incident">
        Atlantique incident
       </a>
       , when two MiG-21 aircraft of the Indian Air Force intercepted and shot down a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breguet_Atlantique" title="Breguet Atlantique">
        Breguet Atlantique
       </a>
       reconnaissance aircraft of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistani_Navy" title="Pakistani Navy">
        Pakistani Navy
       </a>
       with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molniya_R-60" title="Molniya R-60">
        R-60MK
       </a>
       (AA-8 Aphid) air-to-air missile.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Indonesia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AURI_MiG-21.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1120" data-file-width="2288" height="108" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/AURI_MiG-21.png/220px-AURI_MiG-21.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/AURI_MiG-21.png/330px-AURI_MiG-21.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/AURI_MiG-21.png/440px-AURI_MiG-21.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AURI_MiG-21.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Indonesian Air Force MiG-21 in the Air Force Museum
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_Air_Force" title="Indonesian Air Force">
        Indonesian Air Force
       </a>
       purchased 22 MiG-21s. In 1962, 20 MiG-21F-13s and MiG-21Us were received during
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Trikora" title="Operation Trikora">
        Operation Trikora
       </a>
       in the Western New Guinea conflict. Indonesian MiG-21s never fought in any dogfights. Right after the U.S. backed anti-communist forces took over the government, 13 Indonesian MiG-21s were delivered to the U.S. in exchange for T-33, UH-34D, and later, F-5 and OV-10 aircraft. All remaining MiG-21s were grounded and retired due to lack of spare parts and the withdrawal of Soviet maintenance support.
      </p>
      <p>
       The MiGs were added to the
       <a href="/wiki/4477th_Test_and_Evaluation_Squadron" title="4477th Test and Evaluation Squadron">
        4477th Test and Evaluation Squadron
       </a>
       ("Red Eagles"), a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USAF" title="USAF">
        USAF
       </a>
       aggressor squadron at Tonopah Test Range.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam">
        Vietnam
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Vietnam">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1116" data-file-width="1800" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg/220px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg/330px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg/440px-Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21PF_USAF.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         MiG-21F in
         <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force" title="Vietnam People's Air Force">
          Vietnam People's Air Force
         </a>
         markings exhibited at the
         <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_United_States_Air_Force" title="National Museum of the United States Air Force">
          National Museum of the United States Air Force
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="665" data-file-width="1800" height="81" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg/220px-VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg/330px-VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg/440px-VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VPAF_MiG-21_landing_with_chute.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A missile-armed VPAF
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-21_Fishbed" title="MiG-21 Fishbed">
          MiG-21PF
         </a>
         landing.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_(4324).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="626" data-file-width="1012" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_%284324%29.jpg/220px-Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_%284324%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_%284324%29.jpg/330px-Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_%284324%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_%284324%29.jpg/440px-Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_%284324%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force_MIG-21_(4324).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The MiG-21 N. 4324 of the Vietnam People's Air Force. This fighter aircraft, flown by various pilots, was credited for 14 kills during the Vietnam War
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1199" data-file-width="976" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg/220px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg/330px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg/440px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Air_Force_Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-21bis_Lofting-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         MiG-21bis
         <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Air_Force" title="Bulgarian Air Force">
          Bulgarian Air Force
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       As may be seen from its range figures, the MiG-21 was designed for very short
       <a href="/wiki/Ground-controlled_interception" title="Ground-controlled interception">
        ground-controlled interception
       </a>
       (GCI) missions. It became renowned for this type of mission in the skies over
       <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">
        North Vietnam
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first MiG-21s arrived directly from the Soviet Union by ship in April 1966. After being unloaded and assembled
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       they were given to North Vietnam's oldest fighter unit, the 921st
       <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">
        Fighter
       </a>
       Regiment, which had been created on 3 February 1964 as a MiG-17 unit. Because the North Vietnamese Air Force's 923rd FR was newer and less experienced, they would continue to operate MiG-17s while the arrival of the MiG-19s (
       <a href="/wiki/Shenyang_J-6" title="Shenyang J-6">
        J6
       </a>
       versions) from China in 1969 would create North Vietnam's only MiG-19 unit, the 925th FR. On 3 February 1972, North Vietnam commissioned their fourth and last Fighter Regiment created during the war with the Republic of Vietnam, the MiG-21PFM (Type 94) equipped 927th Fighter Regiment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although 13 of North Vietnam's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flying_aces" title="Flying aces">
        flying aces
       </a>
       attained their status while flying the MiG-21 (cf. three in the MiG-17) many
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_People%27s_Air_Force" title="Vietnam People's Air Force">
        North Vietnamese
       </a>
       pilots preferred the MiG-17 because the high
       <a href="/wiki/Wing_loading" title="Wing loading">
        wing loading
       </a>
       of the MiG-21 made it relatively less maneuverable and the lighter framed canopy of the MiG-17 gave better visibility.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, this is not the impression perceived by British author Roger Boniface when he interviewed Pham Ngoc Lan and ace
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nguyen_Nhat_Chieu" title="Nguyen Nhat Chieu">
        Nguyễn Nhật Chiêu
       </a>
       (who scored victories flying both MiG-17 and MiG-21).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Pham Ngoc Lan told Boniface that "The MiG-21 was much faster, and it had two ATOLL missiles which were very accurate and reliable when fired between 1,000 and 1,200 yards."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       And Chiêu asserted that "... for me personally I preferred the MiG-21 because it was superior in all specifications in climb, speed and armament. The ATOLL missile was very accurate and I scored four kills with the ATOLL. ... In general combat conditions I was always confident of a kill over a F-4 Phantom when flying a MiG-21."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although the MiG-21 lacked the long-range radar, missiles, and heavy bomb load of its contemporary multi-mission U.S. fighters, with its
       <a href="/wiki/RP-21_Sapfir" title="RP-21 Sapfir">
        RP-21 Sapfir
       </a>
       radar it proved a challenging adversary in the hands of experienced pilots, especially when used in high-speed hit-and-run attacks under
       <a href="/wiki/Ground-controlled_interception" title="Ground-controlled interception">
        GCI
       </a>
       control. MiG-21 intercepts of
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_F-105_Thunderchief" title="Republic F-105 Thunderchief">
        Republic F-105 Thunderchief
       </a>
       strike groups were effective in downing US aircraft or forcing them to jettison their bomb loads.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="MiG-21_aerial_combat_victories_in_the_Vietnam_War_1966.E2.80.931972">
       </span>

         AA-2 Atoll (
         <a href="/wiki/K-13_(missile)" title="K-13 (missile)">

         </a>
         )
        </td>
